<figure class="mw-halign-right" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Inside_and_Rear_of_Webserver.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Inside_and_Rear_of_Webserver.jpg/330px-Inside_and_Rear_of_Webserver.jpg" decoding="async" width="300" height="200" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Inside_and_Rear_of_Webserver.jpg/500px-Inside_and_Rear_of_Webserver.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Inside_and_Rear_of_Webserver.jpg/960px-Inside_and_Rear_of_Webserver.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3504" data-file-height="2336" /></a><figcaption>The inside and front of a <a href="/wiki/Dell_PowerEdge" class="mw-redirect" title="Dell PowerEdge">Dell PowerEdge</a> server, a computer designed to be mounted in a <a href="/wiki/Rack_mount" class="mw-redirect" title="Rack mount">rack mount</a> environment. Servers similar to this one are often used as web servers.</figcaption></figure>
<figure class="mw-halign-right" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Wikimedia_Foundation_Servers-8055_35.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Wikimedia_Foundation_Servers-8055_35.jpg/330px-Wikimedia_Foundation_Servers-8055_35.jpg" decoding="async" width="300" height="200" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Wikimedia_Foundation_Servers-8055_35.jpg/500px-Wikimedia_Foundation_Servers-8055_35.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Wikimedia_Foundation_Servers-8055_35.jpg/960px-Wikimedia_Foundation_Servers-8055_35.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5184" data-file-height="3456" /></a><figcaption>Multiple web servers may be used for a high-traffic website.</figcaption></figure>
<figure class="mw-halign-right" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Wikimedia_Servers-0051_10.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Wikimedia_Servers-0051_10.jpg/330px-Wikimedia_Servers-0051_10.jpg" decoding="async" width="320" height="213" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Wikimedia_Servers-0051_10.jpg/500px-Wikimedia_Servers-0051_10.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Wikimedia_Servers-0051_10.jpg/960px-Wikimedia_Servers-0051_10.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5616" data-file-height="3744" /></a><figcaption> <a href="/wiki/Server_farm" title="Server farm">Server farm</a> with thousands of web servers used for super-high traffic websites</figcaption></figure>
<figure class="mw-halign-right" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Acorplan120m.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Acorplan120m.jpg/250px-Acorplan120m.jpg" decoding="async" width="160" height="120" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Acorplan120m.jpg/330px-Acorplan120m.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="2448" /></a><figcaption><a href="/wiki/Asymmetric_digital_subscriber_line" class="mw-redirect" title="Asymmetric digital subscriber line">ADSL</a> modem running an <a href="/wiki/Embedded_HTTP_server" title="Embedded HTTP server">embedded web server</a> serving <a href="/wiki/Dynamic_web_page" title="Dynamic web page">dynamic web pages</a> used for modem configuration</figcaption></figure>
<p>A <b>web server</b> is <a href="/wiki/Computer" title="Computer">computer</a> <a href="/wiki/Software" title="Software">software</a> that accepts requests via <a href="/wiki/Hypertext_Transfer_Protocol" class="mw-redirect" title="Hypertext Transfer Protocol">HTTP</a> (the <a href="/wiki/Network_protocol" class="mw-redirect" title="Network protocol">network protocol</a> created to distribute <a href="/wiki/Web_content" title="Web content">web content</a>) or its secure variant <a href="/wiki/HTTPS" title="HTTPS">HTTPS</a>. A user agent, commonly a <a href="/wiki/Web_browser" title="Web browser">web browser</a> or <a href="/wiki/Web_crawler" title="Web crawler">web crawler</a>, initiates communication by making a request for a <a href="/wiki/Web_page" title="Web page">web page</a> or other <a href="/wiki/Web_Resource" class="mw-redirect" title="Web Resource">resource</a> using HTTP, and the <a href="/wiki/Server_(computing)" title="Server (computing)">server</a> responds with the content of that resource or an <a href="/wiki/List_of_HTTP_status_codes" title="List of HTTP status codes">error message</a>. A web server can also accept and store resources sent from the user agent if configured to do so.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-web-server-technology&#95;1-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-web-server-technology-1"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>1<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-web-server-sun&#95;2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-web-server-sun-2"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>2<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>3<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>4<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>5<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The hardware used to run a web server can vary according to the volume of requests that it needs to handle. At the low end of the range are <a href="/wiki/Embedded_system" title="Embedded system">embedded systems</a>, such as a <a href="/wiki/Router_(computing)" title="Router (computing)">router</a> that runs a small web server as its configuration interface. A high-traffic <a href="/wiki/Internet" title="Internet">Internet</a> <a href="/wiki/Website" title="Website">website</a> might handle requests with hundreds of servers that run on racks of high-speed computers.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>6<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>A resource sent from a web server can be a pre-existing <a href="/wiki/Computer_file" title="Computer file">file</a> (<a href="/wiki/Static_web_page" title="Static web page">static content</a>) available to the web server, or it can be generated at the time of the request (<a href="/wiki/Dynamic_web_page" title="Dynamic web page">dynamic content</a>) by another <a href="/wiki/Computer_program" title="Computer program">program</a> that communicates with the server software. The former usually can be served faster and can be more easily <a href="/wiki/Web_cache" title="Web cache">cached</a> for repeated requests, while the latter supports a broader range of applications.
</p><p>Technologies such as <a href="/wiki/Representational_state_transfer" class="mw-redirect" title="Representational state transfer">REST</a> and <a href="/wiki/SOAP" title="SOAP">SOAP</a>, which use HTTP as a basis for general computer-to-computer communication, as well as support for <a href="/wiki/WebDAV" title="WebDAV">WebDAV</a> extensions, have extended the application of web servers well beyond their original purpose of serving human-readable pages.
</p>
<meta property="mw:PageProp/toc" />
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="History">History</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Web_server&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<figure class="mw-halign-right" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Ginevra,_centro_visitatori_del_cern,_primo_server_della_storia_(1989),_02.JPG" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Ginevra%2C_centro_visitatori_del_cern%2C_primo_server_della_storia_%281989%29%2C_02.JPG/120px-Ginevra%2C_centro_visitatori_del_cern%2C_primo_server_della_storia_%281989%29%2C_02.JPG" decoding="async" width="120" height="120" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Ginevra%2C_centro_visitatori_del_cern%2C_primo_server_della_storia_%281989%29%2C_02.JPG/250px-Ginevra%2C_centro_visitatori_del_cern%2C_primo_server_della_storia_%281989%29%2C_02.JPG 1.5x" data-file-width="2352" data-file-height="2346" /></a><figcaption>First web proposal (1989) evaluated as <i>"vague but exciting..."</i></figcaption></figure>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:First_Web_Server.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/First_Web_Server.jpg/250px-First_Web_Server.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="188" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/First_Web_Server.jpg/500px-First_Web_Server.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1536" /></a><figcaption>The world's first web server, a <a href="/wiki/NeXT_Computer" title="NeXT Computer">NeXT Computer</a> workstation with Ethernet, 1990. The case label reads: "This machine is a server. DO NOT POWER IT DOWN!!"</figcaption></figure>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1320445320">.mw-parser-output .hatnote{font-style:italic}.mw-parser-output div.hatnote{padding-left:1.6em;margin-bottom:0.5em}.mw-parser-output .hatnote i{font-style:normal}.mw-parser-output .hatnote+link+.hatnote{margin-top:-0.5em}@media print{body.ns-0 .mw-parser-output .hatnote{display:none!important}}</style><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_web_browser" title="History of the web browser">History of the web browser</a>, <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_World_Wide_Web" title="History of the World Wide Web">History of the World Wide Web</a>, and <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Internet" title="History of the Internet">History of the Internet</a></div>
<p>This is a very brief history of <i>web server programs</i>, so some information necessarily overlaps with the histories of the <i>web browsers</i>, the <i>World Wide Web</i> and the <i>Internet</i>; therefore, for the sake of clarity and understandability, some key historical information below reported may be similar to that found also in one or more of the above-mentioned history articles.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>7<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Initial_WWW_project_(1989–1991)"><span id="Initial_WWW_project_.281989.E2.80.931991.29"></span>Initial WWW project (1989–1991)</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Web_server&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Initial WWW project (1989–1991)"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>In March 1989, <a href="/wiki/Sir_Tim_Berners-Lee" class="mw-redirect" title="Sir Tim Berners-Lee">Sir Tim Berners-Lee</a> proposed a new project to his employer <a href="/wiki/CERN" title="CERN">CERN</a>, with the goal of easing the exchange of information between scientists by using a <a href="/wiki/Hypertext" title="Hypertext">hypertext</a> system. The proposal titled <i>"HyperText and CERN"</i>, asked for comments and it was read by several people. In October 1990 the proposal was reformulated and enriched (having as co-author <a href="/wiki/Robert_Cailliau" title="Robert Cailliau">Robert Cailliau</a>), and finally, it was approved.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-TBL-fight-fake-news&#95;8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TBL-fight-fake-news-8"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>8<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-history-computers-internet-www&#95;9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-history-computers-internet-www-9"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>9<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-www-project-history-original&#95;10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-www-project-history-original-10"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>10<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Between late 1990 and early 1991 the project resulted in Berners-Lee and his developers writing and testing several software libraries along with three programs, which initially ran on <a href="/wiki/NeXTSTEP" title="NeXTSTEP">NeXTSTEP OS</a> installed on <a href="/wiki/NeXT" title="NeXT">NeXT</a> workstations:<sup id="cite&#95;ref-www-TBL-announcement-1991&#95;11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-www-TBL-announcement-1991-11"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>11<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-web-history&#95;12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-web-history-12"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>12<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-www-project-history-original&#95;10-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-www-project-history-original-10"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>10<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<ul><li>a graphical <a href="/wiki/Web_browser" title="Web browser">web browser</a>, called <a href="/wiki/WorldWideWeb" title="WorldWideWeb">WorldWideWeb</a>;</li>
<li>a portable <a href="/wiki/Line_Mode_Browser" title="Line Mode Browser">line mode web browser</a>;</li>
<li>a web server, later known as <a href="/wiki/CERN_httpd" title="CERN httpd">CERN httpd</a>.</li></ul>
<p>Those early browsers retrieved web pages written in a <a href="/wiki/HTML#History" title="HTML">simple early form of HTML</a> from web servers using a new basic communication protocol that was named <a href="/wiki/Hypertext_Transfer_Protocol#History" class="mw-redirect" title="Hypertext Transfer Protocol">HTTP 0.9</a>.
</p><p>In August 1991 Tim Berners-Lee announced the <i>birth of WWW technology</i> and encouraged scientists to adopt and develop it.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-www-TBL-web-announcement&#95;13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-www-TBL-web-announcement-13"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>13<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Soon after, those programs, along with their <a href="/wiki/Source_code" title="Source code">source code</a>, were made available to people interested in their usage.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-www-TBL-announcement-1991&#95;11-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-www-TBL-announcement-1991-11"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>11<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Although the source code was not formally licensed or placed in the public domain, CERN informally allowed users and developers to experiment and further develop on top of them. Berners-Lee started promoting the adoption and the usage of those programs along with their <a href="/wiki/Porting" title="Porting">porting</a> to other <a href="/wiki/Operating_system" title="Operating system">operating systems</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-www-project-history-original&#95;10-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-www-project-history-original-10"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>10<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Fast_and_wild_development_(1991–1995)"><span id="Fast_and_wild_development_.281991.E2.80.931995.29"></span>Fast and wild development (1991–1995)</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Web_server&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Fast and wild development (1991–1995)"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>In December 1991, the <strong>first web server outside Europe</strong> was installed at SLAC (U.S.A.).<sup id="cite&#95;ref-web-history&#95;12-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-web-history-12"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>12<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> This was a very important event because it started trans-continental web communications between web browsers and web servers.
</p><p>In 1991–1993, CERN web server program continued to be actively developed by the www group, meanwhile, thanks to the availability of its source code and the public specifications of the HTTP protocol, many other implementations of web servers started to be developed.
</p><p>In April 1993, CERN issued a public official statement stating that the three components of Web software (the basic line-mode client, the web server and the library of common code), along with their <a href="/wiki/Source_code" title="Source code">source code</a>, were put in the <a href="/wiki/Public_domain" title="Public domain">public domain</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-CERN-licensing-the-web&#95;14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CERN-licensing-the-web-14"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>14<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> This statement freed web server developers from any possible legal issue about the development of <i>derivative work</i> based on that source code (a threat that in practice never existed).
</p><p>
At the beginning of 1994, the most notable among new web servers was <a href="/wiki/NCSA_httpd" class="mw-redirect" title="NCSA httpd">NCSA httpd</a> which ran on a variety of <a href="/wiki/Unix" title="Unix">Unix</a>-based OSs and could serve <i>dynamically generated content</i> by implementing the <code>POST</code> HTTP method and the <a href="/wiki/Common_Gateway_Interface" title="Common Gateway Interface">CGI</a> to communicate with external programs. These capabilities, along with the multimedia features of NCSA's <a href="/wiki/Mosaic_(web_browser)" class="mw-redirect" title="Mosaic (web browser)">Mosaic</a> browser (also able to manage <a href="/wiki/HTML" title="HTML">HTML</a> <a href="/wiki/Form_(HTML)" class="mw-redirect" title="Form (HTML)">FORMs</a> in order to send data to a web server) highlighted the potential of web technology for publishing and <a href="/wiki/Distributed_computing" title="Distributed computing">distributed computing</a> applications.</p><div class="thumb tright" style=""><div class="thumbinner" style="width: fit-content;"><div class="center noresize" style="width: auto;">

dominant-baseline="central" text-anchor="middle" style="font-size:16px;font-family:sans-serif;font-weight:bold;" xml:space="preserve" y="8" transform="translate(200 5)" fill="var(--color-emphasized, #101418)">Number of active web sites (1991–1996)</text><style>.mw-chart-618c7ba70c32bade0faddcca565d6c04703948e11a35e239db1940d3495350115dc62d2dd7946a12b0518e4157a12a00e796b553f04c4c2987d01c59b87d8498__zr3094828-cls-16356440:hover{pointer-events:none}.mw-chart-618c7ba70c32bade0faddcca565d6c04703948e11a35e239db1940d3495350115dc62d2dd7946a12b0518e4157a12a00e796b553f04c4c2987d01c59b87d8498__zr3094828-cls-16356441:hover{cursor:pointer;fill:rgba(82,130,235,1)}.mw-chart-618c7ba70c32bade0faddcca565d6c04703948e11a35e239db1940d3495350115dc62d2dd7946a12b0518e4157a12a00e796b553f04c4c2987d01c59b87d8498__zr3094828-cls-16356442:hover{cursor:pointer;fill:rgba(0,0,0,0)}</style></svg></wiki-chart></div><div class="center"><small><span class="caption enwiki-chart-caption" role="caption" id="enwiki-chart-caption-id"></span> View <a href="https://commons.wikimedia.org/wiki/Data:Number_of_active_web_sites_(1991%E2%80%931996).tab" class="extiw" title="c:Data:Number of active web sites (1991–1996).tab">source data</a>.</small></div></div><div style="clear: both;"></div> </div><div class="thumbcaption">Number of active web sites (1991–1996)<sup id="cite&#95;ref-ws-web-app-test-ajax&#95;15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ws-web-app-test-ajax-15"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>15<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-ws-stats-1991-1996&#95;16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ws-stats-1991-1996-16"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>16<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></div></div></div><p>In the second half of 1994, the development of NCSA httpd stalled to the point that a group of external software developers, <a href="/wiki/Webmaster" title="Webmaster">webmasters</a> and other professional figures interested in that server, started to write and collect <a href="/wiki/Patch_(computing)" title="Patch (computing)">patches</a> thanks to the NCSA httpd source code being available to the public domain. At the beginning of 1995 those patches were all applied to the last release of NCSA source code and, after several tests, the <a href="/wiki/Apache_HTTP_server" class="mw-redirect" title="Apache HTTP server">Apache HTTP server</a> project was started.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-NCSA-public-Apache&#95;17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NCSA-public-Apache-17"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>17<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-ws-apache-how-it-came-to-be&#95;18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ws-apache-how-it-came-to-be-18"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>18<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>At the end of 1994, a new commercial web server, named <a href="/wiki/Oracle_iPlanet_Web_Server#Netsite" title="Oracle iPlanet Web Server">Netsite</a>, was released with specific features. It was the first one of many other similar products that were developed first by <a href="/wiki/Netscape" title="Netscape">Netscape</a>, then also by <a href="/wiki/Sun_Microsystems" title="Sun Microsystems">Sun Microsystems</a>, and finally by <a href="/wiki/Oracle_Corporation" title="Oracle Corporation">Oracle Corporation</a>.
</p><p>In mid-1995, the first version of <a href="/wiki/Internet_Information_Services" title="Internet Information Services">IIS</a> was released by <a href="/wiki/Microsoft" title="Microsoft">Microsoft</a> for <a href="/wiki/Windows_NT" title="Windows NT">Windows NT</a> OS. This marked the entry, in the field of World Wide Web technologies, of a commercial developer and vendor that has played and still is playing a key role on both sides (client and server) of the web.
</p><p>In the second half of 1995, CERN and NCSA web servers started to decline (in global percentage usage) because of the widespread adoption of new web servers which had a much faster development cycle along with more features, more fixes applied, and more performances than the previous ones.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Explosive_growth_and_competition_(1996–2014)"><span id="Explosive_growth_and_competition_.281996.E2.80.932014.29"></span>Explosive growth and competition (1996–2014)</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Web_server&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Explosive growth and competition (1996–2014)"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>

dominant-baseline="central" text-anchor="end" style="font-size:12px;font-family:sans-serif;" transform="translate(166.48 100)" fill="var(--color-subtle, #54595D)">15,000,000</text><text dominant-baseline="central" text-anchor="middle" style="font-size:12px;font-family:sans-serif;" y="6" transform="translate(187.0171 538)" fill="var(--color-subtle, #54595D)">1996</text><text dominant-baseline="central" text-anchor="middle" style="font-size:12px;font-family:sans-serif;" y="6" transform="translate(237.1657 538)" fill="var(--color-subtle, #54595D)">1998</text><text dominant-baseline="central" text-anchor="middle" style="font-size:12px;font-family:sans-serif;" y="6" transform="translate(287.3143 538)" fill="var(--color-subtle, #54595D)">2000</text><text dominant-baseline="central" text-anchor="middle" style="font-size:12px;font-family:sans-serif;" y="6" transform="translate(337.4629 538)" fill="var(--color-subtle, #54595D)">2002</text><path d="M178.4 dominant-baseline="central" text-anchor="middle" style="font-size:16px;font-family:sans-serif;font-weight:bold;" xml:space="preserve" y="8" transform="translate(200 5)" fill="var(--color-emphasized, #101418)">Number of active web sites class="center"><small><span class="caption enwiki-chart-caption" role="caption" id="enwiki-chart-caption-id"></span> View <a href="https://commons.wikimedia.org/wiki/Data:Number_of_active_web_sites_(1996-2002).tab" class="extiw" title="c:Data:Number of active web sites (1996-2002).tab">source data</a>.</small></div></div><div style="clear: both;"></div> </div><div class="thumbcaption">Number of active web sites (1996-2002)<sup id="cite&#95;ref-ws-stats-1991-1996&#95;16-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ws-stats-1991-1996-16"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>16<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-ws-stats-1999-2002&#95;19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ws-stats-1999-2002-19"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>19<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></div></div></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-right" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Cobalt_Qube_3_Front.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Cobalt_Qube_3_Front.jpg/250px-Cobalt_Qube_3_Front.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="188" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Cobalt_Qube_3_Front.jpg/500px-Cobalt_Qube_3_Front.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1200" /></a><figcaption>Sun's <a href="/wiki/Cobalt_Qube" title="Cobalt Qube">Cobalt Qube</a> 3 – a computer <a href="/wiki/Server_appliance" class="mw-redirect" title="Server appliance">server appliance</a> (2002, discontinued)</figcaption></figure>
<p>At the end of 1996, there were already over fifty known, different web-server-software programs that were available to everybody who wanted to own an Internet <a href="/wiki/Domain_name" title="Domain name">domain name</a> or to host websites.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-ws-1996-sw-products&#95;20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ws-1996-sw-products-20"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>20<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Many of them lived only shortly and were replaced by other web servers.
</p><p>The publication of <a href="/wiki/Request_for_Comments" title="Request for Comments">RFCs</a> about protocol versions HTTP/1.0 (1996) and HTTP/1.1 (1997, 1999), forced most web servers to comply (not always completely) with those standards. The use of TCP/IP <a href="/wiki/HTTP_persistent_connection" title="HTTP persistent connection">persistent connections</a> (HTTP/1.1) required web servers both to increase the maximum number of concurrent connections allowed and to improve their level of scalability.
</p><p>Between 1996 and 1999, <a href="/wiki/Netscape_Application_Server" title="Netscape Application Server">Netscape Enterprise Server</a> and Microsoft's IIS emerged among the leading commercial options whereas among the freely available and <a href="/wiki/Open-source" class="mw-redirect" title="Open-source">open-source</a> programs Apache HTTP Server held the lead as the preferred server (because of its reliability and its many features).
</p><p>In those years there was also another commercial web server called <a href="/wiki/Zeus_Web_Server" title="Zeus Web Server">Zeus</a> (<i>now discontinued</i>) that was known as one of the fastest and most scalable web servers available on market, at least till the first decade of 2000s, despite its low percentage of usage.
</p><p>Apache resulted in the most used web server from mid-1996 to the end of 2015 when, after a few years of decline, it was surpassed initially by IIS and then by Nginx. Afterward IIS dropped to much lower percentages of usage than Apache (see also <a href="#Market_share">market share</a>).
</p><p>From 2005–2006, Apache started to improve its speed and its scalability level by introducing new performance features (e.g., event MPM and new content cache).<sup id="cite&#95;ref-ws-apache-overview-2.2&#95;21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ws-apache-overview-2.2-21"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>21<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-ws-apache-overview-2.4&#95;22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ws-apache-overview-2.4-22"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>22<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> As those new performance improvements initially were marked as experimental, they were not enabled by its users for a long time and so Apache suffered, even more, the competition of commercial servers and, above all, of other open-source servers which meanwhile had already achieved far superior performances (mostly when serving static content) since the beginning of their development and at the time of the Apache decline were able to offer also a long enough list of well tested advanced features.
</p><p>A few years after 2000 started, not only other commercial and highly competitive web servers (e.g., <a href="/wiki/LiteSpeed_Web_Server" title="LiteSpeed Web Server">LiteSpeed</a>) but also many other open-source programs such as <a href="/wiki/Hiawatha_(web_server)" title="Hiawatha (web server)">Hiawatha</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cherokee_(webserver)" class="mw-redirect" title="Cherokee (webserver)">Cherokee HTTP server</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lighttpd" title="Lighttpd">Lighttpd</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nginx" title="Nginx">Nginx</a> and other derived and related products also available with commercial support emerged.
</p><p>Around 2007–2008, most popular web browsers increased their previous default limit of 2 persistent connections per host-domain (a limit recommended by RFC-2616)<sup id="cite&#95;ref-rfc2616-8.1.4&#95;23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rfc2616-8.1.4-23"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>23<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> to 4, 6 or 8 persistent connections per host-domain, in order to speed up the retrieval of heavy web pages with lots of images, and to mitigate the problem of the shortage of persistent connections dedicated to dynamic objects used for bi-directional notifications of events in web pages.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-browsers-max-persistent-connections-per-host-domain&#95;24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-browsers-max-persistent-connections-per-host-domain-24"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>24<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Within a year, these changes, on average, nearly tripled the maximum number of persistent connections that web servers had to manage. This trend (of increasing the number of persistent connections) definitely gave a strong impetus to the adoption of <a href="/wiki/Reverse_proxy" title="Reverse proxy">reverse proxies</a> in front of slower web servers and it gave also one more chance to the emerging new web servers that could show all their speed and their capability to handle very high numbers of concurrent connections without requiring too many hardware resources (expensive computers with lots of CPUs, RAM and fast disks).<sup id="cite&#95;ref-ws-root-bench-2016&#95;25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ws-root-bench-2016-25"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>25<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="New_challenges_(2015_and_later_years)"><span id="New_challenges_.282015_and_later_years.29"></span>New challenges (2015 and later years)</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Web_server&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: New challenges (2015 and later years)"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>In 2015, RFCs published new protocol version [HTTP/2], and as the implementation of new specifications was not trivial at all, a <b>dilemma arose among developers of less popular web servers</b> (e.g., with a percentage of usage lower than 1% .. 2%), about adding or not adding support for that new protocol version.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-http2-faq-http2-replace-http1&#95;26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-http2-faq-http2-replace-http1-26"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>26<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-ws-http2-support&#95;27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ws-http2-support-27"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>27<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In fact supporting HTTP/2 often required radical changes to their internal implementation due to many factors (practically always required encrypted connections, capability to distinguish between HTTP/1.x and HTTP/2 connections on the same TCP port, binary representation of HTTP messages, message priority, compression of HTTP headers, use of streams also known as TCP/IP sub-connections and related flow-control, etc.) and so a few developers of those web servers opted for <a href="/wiki/Comparison_of_web_server_software#Features" title="Comparison of web server software">not supporting new HTTP/2 version</a> (at least in the near future) also because of these main reasons:<sup id="cite&#95;ref-http2-faq-http2-replace-http1&#95;26-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-http2-faq-http2-replace-http1-26"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>26<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-ws-http2-support&#95;27-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ws-http2-support-27"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>27<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<ul><li>protocols HTTP/1.x would have been supported anyway by browsers for a very long time (maybe forever) so that there would be no incompatibility between clients and servers in next future;</li>
<li>implementing HTTP/2 was considered a task of <a href="/wiki/HTTP/2#Criticisms" title="HTTP/2">overwhelming complexity</a> that could open the door to a whole new class of <a href="/wiki/Software_bug" title="Software bug">bugs</a> that till 2015 did not exist and so it would have required notable investments in developing and testing the implementation of the new protocol;</li>
<li>adding HTTP/2 support could always be done in future in case the efforts would be justified.</li></ul>
<p>Instead, developers of <b>most popular web servers, rushed to offer the availability of new protocol</b>, not only because they had the work force and the time to do so, but also because usually their previous implementation of <a href="/wiki/SPDY" title="SPDY">SPDY</a> protocol could be reused as a starting point and because most used web browsers implemented it very quickly for the same reason. Another reason that prompted those developers to act quickly was that webmasters felt the pressure of the ever increasing <a href="/wiki/Web_traffic" title="Web traffic">web traffic</a> and they really wanted to install and to try – as soon as possible – something that could drastically lower the number of TCP/IP connections and speedup accesses to hosted websites.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-http2-faq-just-1-connection&#95;28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-http2-faq-just-1-connection-28"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>28<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In 2020–2021 the HTTP/2 dynamics about its implementation (by top web servers and popular web browsers) were partly replicated after the publication of advanced drafts of future RFC about <a href="/wiki/HTTP/3" title="HTTP/3">HTTP/3</a> protocol.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Technical_overview">Technical overview</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Web_server&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Technical overview"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<figure class="mw-halign-right" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Client-server-model.svg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Client-server-model.svg/250px-Client-server-model.svg.png" decoding="async" width="250" height="150" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Client-server-model.svg/500px-Client-server-model.svg.png 1.5x" data-file-width="500" data-file-height="300" /></a><figcaption>PC clients connected to a web server via Internet</figcaption></figure>
<p>The following technical overview should be considered only as an attempt to give a few very <i>limited examples</i> about <i>some</i> features that may be <a href="/wiki/Implementation#Computer_science" title="Implementation">implemented</a> in a web server and <i>some</i> of the tasks that it may perform in order to have a sufficiently wide scenario about the topic.
</p><p>A <b>web server program</b> plays the role of a server in a <a href="/wiki/Client%E2%80%93server_model" title="Client–server model">client–server model</a> by implementing one or more versions of HTTP protocol, often including the HTTPS secure variant and other features and extensions that are considered useful for its planned usage.
</p><p>The complexity and the efficiency of a web server program may vary a lot depending on:<sup id="cite&#95;ref-web-server-technology&#95;1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-web-server-technology-1"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>1<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<ul><li><a href="#Common_features">common features</a> implemented;</li>
<li><a href="#Common_tasks">common tasks</a> performed;</li>
<li><a href="#Performances">performances</a> and scalability level aimed as a goal;</li>
<li><a href="#Software_efficiency">software</a> model and techniques adopted to achieve wished performance and scalability level;</li>
<li>target hardware and category of usage (e.g., embedded system, low-medium traffic web server, high traffic <a href="/wiki/Internet" title="Internet">Internet</a> web server).</li></ul>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Common_features">Common features</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Web_server&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Common features"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>Although web server programs differ in how they are implemented, most of them offer the following common features.
</p><p>These are <b>basic features</b> that most web servers usually have.
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Static_web_page" title="Static web page">Static content serving</a>: to be able to serve static content (web files) to clients via HTTP protocol.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/HTTP" title="HTTP">HTTP</a>: support for one or more versions of HTTP protocol in order to send versions of HTTP responses compatible with versions of client HTTP requests, (e.g., HTTP/1.0, HTTP/1.1, <a href="/wiki/HTTP/2" title="HTTP/2">HTTP/2</a>, <a href="/wiki/HTTP/3" title="HTTP/3">HTTP/3</a>).</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Logging_(software)" class="mw-redirect" title="Logging (software)">Logging</a>: usually web servers have also the capability of logging some information, about client requests and server responses, to <a href="/wiki/Server_log" class="mw-redirect" title="Server log">log files</a> for security and statistical purposes.</li></ul>
<p>A few other more <b>advanced</b> and popular <b>features</b> (<i>only a very short selection</i>) are the following ones.
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Dynamic_web_page" title="Dynamic web page">Dynamic content serving</a>: to be able to serve dynamic content (generated on the fly) to clients via HTTP protocol.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Virtual_hosting" title="Virtual hosting">Virtual hosting</a>: to be able to serve many websites (<a href="/wiki/Domain_name" title="Domain name">domain names</a>) using only one <a href="/wiki/IP_address" title="IP address">IP address</a>.</li>
<li><a href="#URL_authorization">Authorization</a>: to be able to allow, to forbid or to authorize access to portions of website paths (web resources).</li>
<li><a href="#Content_cache">Content cache</a>: to be able to cache content in order to speed up server responses;</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Large_file_support" class="mw-redirect" title="Large file support">Large file support</a>: to be able to serve files whose size is greater than 2 GB on 32 bit <a href="/wiki/Operating_system" title="Operating system">OS</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Bandwidth_throttling" title="Bandwidth throttling">Bandwidth throttling</a>: to limit the speed of content responses in order to not saturate the network and to be able to serve more clients;</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Rewrite_engine" title="Rewrite engine">Rewrite engine</a>: to map parts of <a href="/wiki/Clean_URL" title="Clean URL">clean URLs</a> (found in client requests) to their real names.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Custom_error_page" class="mw-redirect" title="Custom error page">Custom error pages</a>: support for customized HTTP error messages.</li></ul>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Common_tasks">Common tasks</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Web_server&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Common tasks"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>A web server program, when it is running, usually performs several general <b>tasks</b>:<sup id="cite&#95;ref-web-server-technology&#95;1-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-web-server-technology-1"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>1<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<ul><li>starts, optionally reads and applies settings found in its <a href="/wiki/Configuration_file" title="Configuration file">configuration files</a> or elsewhere, optionally opens log file, starts listening to client connections and requests;</li>
<li>optionally tries to adapt its general behavior according to its settings and its current <a href="#Operating_conditions">operating conditions</a>;</li>
<li>manages <b>client connections</b> (accepting new ones or closing the existing ones as required);</li>
<li><b><a href="#Read_request_message">receives</a></b> client requests (by reading HTTP messages):
<ul><li>reads and verify each HTTP request message;</li>
<li>usually performs <a href="#URL_normalization">URL normalization</a>;</li>
<li>usually performs <a href="#URL_mapping">URL mapping</a> (which may default to URL path translation);</li>
<li>usually performs <a href="#URL_path_translation_to_file_system">URL path translation</a> along with various security checks;</li></ul></li>
<li><b><a href="#Manage_request_message">executes</a></b> or refuses requested HTTP method:
<ul><li>optionally manages <a href="#URL_authorization">URL authorizations</a>;</li>
<li>optionally manages <a href="#URL_redirection">URL redirections</a>;</li>
<li>optionally manages requests for <b><a href="#Serve_static_content">static resources</a></b> (file contents):
<ul><li>optionally manages <a href="#Directory_index_files">directory index files</a>;</li>
<li>optionally manages <a href="#Regular_files">regular files</a>;</li></ul></li>
<li>optionally manages requests for <b><a href="#Serve_dynamic_content">dynamic resources</a></b>:
<ul><li>optionally manages <a href="#Directory_listings">directory listings</a>;</li>
<li>optionally manages <a href="#Program_or_module_processing">program or module processing</a>, checking the availability, the start and eventually the stop of the execution of external programs used to generate dynamic content;</li>
<li>optionally manages the communications with external programs or internal modules used to generate dynamic content;</li></ul></li></ul></li>
<li><b><a href="#Send_response_message">replies</a></b> to client requests sending proper HTTP responses (e.g., requested resources or error messages) eventually verifying or adding <a href="/wiki/HTTP_headers" class="mw-redirect" title="HTTP headers">HTTP headers</a> to those sent by dynamic programs and modules;</li>
<li>optionally <b>logs</b> (partially or totally) <b>client requests or its responses</b> to an external user log file or to a system log file by <a href="/wiki/Syslog" title="Syslog">syslog</a>, usually using <a href="/wiki/Common_Log_Format" title="Common Log Format">common log format</a>;</li>
<li>optionally <b>logs process messages</b> about <b>detected anomalies or other notable events</b> (e.g., in client requests or in its internal functioning) using syslog or some other system facilities; these log messages usually have a debug, warning, error, alert level which can be filtered (not logged) depending on some settings, see also <a href="/wiki/Syslog#Severity_level" title="Syslog">severity level</a>;</li>
<li>optionally generates <b>statistics</b> about web traffic managed or its performances;</li>
<li>other custom tasks.</li></ul>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Read_request_message">Read request message</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Web_server&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Read request message"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>Web server programs are able:<sup id="cite&#95;ref-rfc7230-2.1&#95;29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rfc7230-2.1-29"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>29<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
<sup id="cite&#95;ref-rfc7230-3.4&#95;30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rfc7230-3.4-30"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>30<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
<sup id="cite&#95;ref-rfc7230-3.5&#95;31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rfc7230-3.5-31"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>31<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<ul><li>to read an HTTP request message;</li>
<li>to interpret it;</li>
<li>to verify its syntax;</li>
<li>to identify known <a href="/wiki/HTTP_headers" class="mw-redirect" title="HTTP headers">HTTP headers</a> and to extract their values from them.</li></ul>
<p>Once an HTTP request message has been decoded and verified, its values can be used to determine whether that request can be satisfied or not. This requires many other steps, including <b><a href="/wiki/Computer_security" title="Computer security">security checks</a></b>.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="URL_normalization">URL normalization</h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Web_server&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: URL normalization"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1320445320" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/URL_normalization" class="mw-redirect" title="URL normalization">URL normalization</a></div>
<p>Web server programs usually perform some type of <a href="/wiki/URL_normalization" class="mw-redirect" title="URL normalization">URL normalization</a> (<a href="/wiki/Uniform_Resource_Locator" class="mw-redirect" title="Uniform Resource Locator">URL</a> found in most HTTP request messages) in order to:
</p>
<ul><li>make resource path always a clean uniform path from root directory of website;</li>
<li>lower security risks (e.g., by intercepting more easily attempts to access static resources outside the root directory of the website or to access to portions of path below website root directory that are forbidden or which require authorization);</li>
<li>make path of web resources more recognizable by human beings and <a href="/wiki/Web_log_analysis_software" title="Web log analysis software">web log analysis programs</a> (also known as log analyzers or statistical applications).</li></ul>
<p>The term <i>URL normalization</i> refers to the process of modifying and standardizing a URL in a consistent manner. There are several types of normalization that may be performed, including the conversion of the scheme and host to lowercase. Among the most important normalizations are the removal of "." and ".." path segments and adding trailing slashes to a non-empty path component.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="URL_mapping">URL mapping</h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Web_server&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: URL mapping"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1305433154" /><table class="box-Update plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Update" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div class="mbox-image-div"><span typeof="mw:File"><span><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Ambox_current_red_Asia_Australia.svg/60px-Ambox_current_red_Asia_Australia.svg.png" decoding="async" width="42" height="34" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Ambox_current_red_Asia_Australia.svg/120px-Ambox_current_red_Asia_Australia.svg.png 1.5x" data-file-width="360" data-file-height="290" /></span></span></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section needs to be <b>updated</b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help update this article to reflect recent events or newly available information.</span>  <span class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">June 2023</span>)</i></span></div></td></tr></tbody></table><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1320445320" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/URL_mapping" class="mw-redirect" title="URL mapping">URL mapping</a></div>
<blockquote><p>"URL mapping is the process by which a web server or application framework determines how an incoming URL request is routed to the appropriate resource, handler, or action. Modern URL mapping mechanisms analyse the structure of the requested URL and use routing rules or configuration patterns to deliver static resources, invoke dynamic handlers, or perform rewrites and redirects without directly relying on file system paths. This approach allows clean, human-readable URLs and flexible application architectures.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>32<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></p></blockquote><p>In practice, web server programs that implement advanced features, beyond the simple <i>static content serving</i> (e.g., URL rewrite engine, dynamic content serving), usually have to figure out how that URL has to be handled as a:
</p><ul><li><a href="#URL_redirection">URL redirection</a>, a redirection to another URL;</li>
<li><i>static request</i> of <a href="/wiki/Computer_file" title="Computer file">file</a> content;</li>
<li><i>dynamic request</i> of:
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Directory_(computing)" title="Directory (computing)">directory</a> listing of files or other sub-directories contained in that directory;</li>
<li>other types of dynamic request in order to identify the program or module processor able to handle that kind of URL path and to pass to it other <a href="/wiki/URL_parts" class="mw-redirect" title="URL parts">URL parts</a>, (i.e., usually path-info and <a href="/wiki/Query_string" title="Query string">query string</a> variables).</li></ul></li></ul>
<p>One or more configuration files of web server may specify the mapping of parts of <b>URL path</b> (e.g., initial parts of <a href="/wiki/Path_(computing)" title="Path (computing)">file path</a>, <a href="/wiki/Filename_extension" title="Filename extension">filename extension</a> and other path components) to a specific URL handler (file, directory, external program or internal module).<sup id="cite&#95;ref-ws-static-rqs-root-dir&#95;33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ws-static-rqs-root-dir-33"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>33<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>When a web server implements one or more of the above-mentioned advanced features then the path part of a valid URL may not always match an existing file system path under website directory tree (a file or a directory in <a href="/wiki/File_system" title="File system">file system</a>) because it can refer to a virtual name of an internal or external module processor for dynamic requests.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="URL_path_translation_to_file_system">URL path translation to file system</h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Web_server&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: URL path translation to file system"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>Web server programs are able to translate an URL path (all or part of it), that refers to a physical file system path, to an <a href="/wiki/Path_(computing)" title="Path (computing)">absolute path</a> under the target website's root directory.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-ws-static-rqs-root-dir&#95;33-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ws-static-rqs-root-dir-33"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>33<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Website's root directory may be specified by a configuration file or by some internal rule of the web server by using the name of the website which is the <a href="/wiki/URL#Syntax" title="URL">host</a> part of the URL found in HTTP client request.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-ws-static-rqs-root-dir&#95;33-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ws-static-rqs-root-dir-33"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>33<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Path translation to file system is done for the following types of web resources:
</p>
<ul><li>a local, usually non-executable, file (static request for file content);</li>
<li>a local directory (dynamic request: directory listing generated on the fly);</li>
<li>a program name (dynamic requests that is executed using CGI or SCGI interface and whose output is read by web server and resent to client who made the HTTP request).</li></ul>
<p>The web server appends the path found in requested URL (HTTP request message) and appends it to the path of the (Host) website root directory. On an <a href="/wiki/Apache_HTTP_Server" title="Apache HTTP Server">Apache server</a>, this is commonly <code>/home/www/website</code> (on <a href="/wiki/Unix" title="Unix">Unix</a> machines, usually it is: <code>/var/www/website</code>). See the following examples of how it may result.
</p><p><b>URL path translation for a static file request</b>
</p><p>Example of a <i>static request</i> of an existing file specified by the following URL:
</p>
<pre>http://www.example.com/path/file.html
</pre>
<p>The client's <a href="/wiki/User_agent" title="User agent">user agent</a> connects to <code>www.example.com</code> and then sends the following <a href="/wiki/HTTP" title="HTTP">HTTP</a>/1.1 request:
</p>
<pre>GET /path/file.html HTTP/1.1
Host: www.example.com
Connection: keep-alive
</pre>
<p>The result is the local file system resource:
</p>
<pre>/home/www/www.example.com/path/file.html
</pre>
<p>The web server then reads the <a href="/wiki/Computer_file" title="Computer file">file</a>, if it exists, and sends a response to the client's web browser. The response will describe the content of the file and contain the file itself or an error message will return saying that the file does not exist or its access is forbidden.
</p><p><b>URL path translation for a directory request (without a static index file)</b>
</p><p>Example of an implicit <i>dynamic request</i> of an existing directory specified by the following URL:
</p>
<pre>http://www.example.com/directory1/directory2/
</pre>
<p>The client's <a href="/wiki/User_agent" title="User agent">user agent</a> connects to <code>www.example.com</code> and then sends the following <a href="/wiki/HTTP" title="HTTP">HTTP</a>/1.1 request:
</p>
<pre>GET /directory1/directory2 HTTP/1.1
Host: www.example.com
Connection: keep-alive
</pre>
<p>The result is the local directory path:
</p>
<pre>/home/www/www.example.com/directory1/directory2/
</pre>
<p>The web server then verifies the existence of the <a href="/wiki/Directory_(computing)" title="Directory (computing)">directory</a> and if it exists and it can be accessed then tries to find out an index file (which in this case does not exist) and so it passes the request to an internal module or a program dedicated to directory listings and finally reads data output and sends a response to the client's web browser. The response will describe the content of the directory (list of contained subdirectories and files) or an error message will return saying that the directory does not exist or its access is forbidden.
</p><p><b>URL path translation for a dynamic program request</b>
</p><p>For a <i>dynamic request</i> the URL path specified by the client should refer to an existing external program (usually an executable file with a CGI) used by the web server to generate dynamic content.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-ws-dynamic-rqs-root-dir&#95;34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ws-dynamic-rqs-root-dir-34"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>34<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Example of a <i>dynamic request</i> using a program file to generate output:
</p>
<pre>http://www.example.com/cgi-bin/forum.php?action=view&amp;orderby=thread&amp;date=2021-10-15
</pre>
<p>The client's <a href="/wiki/User_agent" title="User agent">user agent</a> connects to <code>www.example.com</code> and then sends the following <a href="/wiki/HTTP" title="HTTP">HTTP</a>/1.1 request:
</p>
<pre>GET /cgi-bin/forum.php?action=view&amp;ordeby=thread&amp;date=2021-10-15 HTTP/1.1
Host: www.example.com
Connection: keep-alive
</pre>
<p>The result is the local file path of the program (in this example, a <a href="/wiki/PHP" title="PHP">PHP</a> program):
</p>
<pre>/home/www/www.example.com/cgi-bin/forum.php
</pre>
<p>The web server executes that program, passing in the path-info and the <a href="/wiki/Query_string" title="Query string">query string</a> <code>action=view&amp;orderby=thread&amp;date=2021-10-15</code> so that the program has the info it needs to run. (In this case, it will return an HTML document containing a view of forum entries ordered by thread from October 15, 2021). In addition to this, the web server reads data sent from the external program and resends that data to the client that made the request.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Manage_request_message">Manage request message</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Web_server&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Manage request message"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>Once a request has been read, interpreted, and verified, it has to be managed depending on its method, its URL, and its parameters, which may include values of HTTP headers.
</p><p>In practice, the web server has to handle the request by using one of these response paths:<sup id="cite&#95;ref-ws-static-rqs-root-dir&#95;33-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ws-static-rqs-root-dir-33"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>33<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<ul><li>if something in request was not acceptable (in status line or message headers), web server already sent an error response;</li>
<li>if request has a method (e.g., <code>OPTIONS</code>) that can be satisfied by general code of web server then a successful response is sent;</li>
<li>if URL requires authorization then an <a href="#URL_authorization">authorization error message</a> is sent;</li>
<li>if URL maps to a redirection then a <a href="#URL_redirection">redirect message</a> is sent;</li>
<li>if URL maps to a <a href="#Serve_dynamic_content">dynamic resource</a> (a virtual path or a directory listing) then its handler (an internal module or an external program) is called and request parameters (query string and path info) are passed to it in order to allow it to reply to that request;</li>
<li>if URL maps to a <a href="#Serve_static_content">static resource</a> (usually a file on file system) then the internal static handler is called to send that file;</li>
<li>if request method is not known or if there is some other unacceptable condition (e.g., resource not found, internal server error, etc.) then an <a href="#Error_message">error response</a> is sent.</li></ul>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Serve_static_content">Serve static content</h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Web_server&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Serve static content"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<figure class="mw-halign-right" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Web_server_serving_static_content.png" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Web_server_serving_static_content.png/250px-Web_server_serving_static_content.png" decoding="async" width="221" height="143" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/1/1e/Web_server_serving_static_content.png 1.5x" data-file-width="441" data-file-height="286" /></a><figcaption>PC clients communicating via network with a web server serving static content only</figcaption></figure>
<p>If a web server program is capable of <b>serving static content</b> and it has been configured to do so, then it is able to send file content whenever a request message has a valid URL path matching (after URL mapping, URL translation and URL redirection) that of an existing file under the root directory of a website and file has attributes which match those required by internal rules of web server program.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-ws-static-rqs-root-dir&#95;33-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ws-static-rqs-root-dir-33"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>33<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>That kind of content is called <i>static</i> because usually it is not changed by the web server when it is sent to clients and because it remains the same until it is modified (file modification) by some program.
</p><p>NOTE: when serving <b>static content only</b>, a web server program usually <b>does not change file contents</b> of served websites (as they are only read and never written) and so it suffices to support only these <a href="/wiki/HTTP_method" class="mw-redirect" title="HTTP method">HTTP methods</a>:
</p>
<ul><li><code>OPTIONS</code></li>
<li><code>HEAD</code></li>
<li><code>GET</code></li></ul>
<p>Response of static file content can be sped up by a <b><a href="#File_cache">file cache</a></b>.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading5"><h5 id="Directory_index_files">Directory index files</h5><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Web_server&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Directory index files"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1320445320" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Web_server_directory_index" title="Web server directory index">Web server directory index</a></div>
<p>If a web server program receives a client request message with an URL whose path matches one of an existing <i>directory</i> and that directory is accessible and serving directory index files is enabled then a web server program may try to serve the first of known (or configured) static index file names (a <a href="#Regular_files">regular file</a>) found in that directory; if no index file is found or other conditions are not met then an error message is returned.
</p><p>Most used names for static index files are: <code>index.html</code>, <code>index.htm</code> and <code>Default.htm</code>.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading5"><h5 id="Regular_files">Regular files</h5><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Web_server&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Regular files"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>If a web server program receives a client request message with an URL whose path matches the file name of an existing <i>file</i> and that file is accessible by web server program and its attributes match internal rules of web server program, then web server program can send that file to client.
</p><p>Usually, for security reasons, most web server programs are pre-configured to serve only <a href="/wiki/Regular_file" class="mw-redirect" title="Regular file">regular files</a> or to avoid to use <i>special file types</i> like <a href="/wiki/Device_file" title="Device file">device files</a>, along with <a href="/wiki/Symbolic_link" title="Symbolic link">symbolic links</a> or <a href="/wiki/Hard_link" title="Hard link">hard links</a> to them. The aim is to avoid undesirable side effects when serving static web resources.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-web-server-http&#95;35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-web-server-http-35"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>35<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Serve_dynamic_content">Serve dynamic content</h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Web_server&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Serve dynamic content"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<figure class="mw-halign-right" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Web_server_serving_static_and_dynamic_content.png" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Web_server_serving_static_and_dynamic_content.png/250px-Web_server_serving_static_and_dynamic_content.png" decoding="async" width="221" height="91" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Web_server_serving_static_and_dynamic_content.png/500px-Web_server_serving_static_and_dynamic_content.png 1.5x" data-file-width="731" data-file-height="301" /></a><figcaption>PC clients communicating via network with a web server serving static and dynamic content</figcaption></figure>
<p>If a web server program is capable of <b>serving dynamic content</b> and it has been configured to do so, then it is able to communicate with the proper internal module or external program (associated with the requested URL path) in order to pass to it the parameters of the client request. After that, the web server program reads from it its data response (that it has generated, often on the fly) and then it resends it to the client program who made the request.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2021)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>NOTE: when serving <b>static and dynamic content</b>, a web server program usually has to support also the following HTTP method in order to be able to safely <b>receive data</b> from clients and so to be able to host also websites with interactive forms that may send large data sets (e.g., lots of <a href="/wiki/Data_entry" title="Data entry">data entry</a> or <a href="/wiki/File_upload" class="mw-redirect" title="File upload">file uploads</a>) to web server, external programs or modules:
</p>
<ul><li><code>POST</code></li></ul>
<p>In order to be able to communicate with its internal modules or external programs, a web server program must have implemented one or more of the many available <b>gateway interfaces</b> (see also <a href="#StandardCGIs">Web Server Gateway Interfaces used for dynamic content</a>).
</p><p>The three <b>standard</b> and historical <b>gateway interfaces</b> are the following ones.
</p>
<dl><dt><a href="/wiki/Common_Gateway_Interface" title="Common Gateway Interface">CGI</a></dt>
<dd>An external CGI program is run by web server program for each dynamic request, then web server program reads from it the generated data response and then resends it to client.</dd></dl>
<dl><dt><a href="/wiki/Simple_Common_Gateway_Interface" title="Simple Common Gateway Interface">SCGI</a></dt>
<dd>An external SCGI program (it usually is a process) is started once by web server program or by some other program or process and then it waits for network connections; every time there is a new request for it, web server program makes a new network connection to it in order to send request parameters and to read its data response, then network connection is closed.</dd></dl>
<dl><dt><a href="/wiki/FastCGI" title="FastCGI">FastCGI</a></dt>
<dd>An external FastCGI program (it usually is a process) is started once by web server program or by some other program or process and then it waits for a network connection which is established permanently by web server; through that connection are sent the request parameters and read data responses.</dd></dl>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading5"><h5 id="Directory_listings">Directory listings</h5><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Web_server&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Directory listings"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<figure class="mw-halign-right" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Web_server_directory_list.png" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Web_server_directory_list.png/330px-Web_server_directory_list.png" decoding="async" width="271" height="161" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Web_server_directory_list.png/500px-Web_server_directory_list.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/3/3e/Web_server_directory_list.png 2x" data-file-width="541" data-file-height="321" /></a><figcaption>Directory listing dynamically generated by a web server</figcaption></figure>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1320445320" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Web_server_directory_index" title="Web server directory index">Web server directory index</a></div>
<p>A web server program may be capable to manage the dynamic generation (on the fly) of a <b><a href="/wiki/Web_server_directory_index" title="Web server directory index">directory index list</a></b> of files and sub-directories.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-ws-directory-listings&#95;36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ws-directory-listings-36"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>36<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>If a web server program is configured to do so and a requested URL path matches an existing directory and its access is allowed and no static index file is found under that directory then a web page (usually in HTML format), containing the list of files or subdirectories of above mentioned directory, is <i>dynamically generated</i> (on the fly). If it cannot be generated an error is returned.
</p><p>Some web server programs allow the customization of directory listings by allowing the usage of a web page template—an HTML document containing placeholders, (e.g., <code>$(FILE_NAME), $(FILE_SIZE)</code>, etc.) that are replaced with the field values of each file entry found in directory by web server (e.g., <code>index.tpl</code>) or the usage of HTML and embedded source code that is interpreted and executed (e.g.,, <code>index.asp</code>) or by supporting the usage of dynamic index programs such as CGIs, SCGIs, FCGIs (e.g., <code>index.cgi</code>, <code>index.php</code>, <code>index.fcgi</code>).
</p><p>Usage of dynamically generated <i>directory listings</i> is usually avoided or limited to a few selected directories of a website because that generation takes much more OS resources than sending a static index page.
</p><p>The main usage of <i>directory listings</i> is to allow the download of files (usually when their names, sizes, modification date-times or <a href="/wiki/File_attribute" title="File attribute">file attributes</a> may change randomly and frequently) <i>as they are, without requiring to provide further information to requesting user</i>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-ws-apache-dir&#95;37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ws-apache-dir-37"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>37<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading5"><h5 id="Program_or_module_processing">Program or module processing</h5><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Web_server&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Program or module processing"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>An external program or an internal module (<i>processing unit</i>) can execute some sort of application function that may be used to get data from or to store data to one or more <a href="/wiki/Content_repository" title="Content repository">data repositories</a>:<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2021)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p>
<ul><li>files (file system);</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Database" title="Database">databases</a> (DBs);</li>
<li>other sources located in local computer or in other computers.</li></ul>
<p>A <i>processing unit</i> can return any kind of web content, also by using data retrieved from a data repository:<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2021)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p>
<ul><li>a document (e.g., <a href="/wiki/HTML" title="HTML">HTML</a>, <a href="/wiki/XML" title="XML">XML</a>, etc.);</li>
<li>an image;</li>
<li>a video;</li>
<li>structured data (e.g., that may be used to update one or more values displayed by a dynamic page (<a href="/wiki/DHTML" class="mw-redirect" title="DHTML">DHTML</a>) of a <a href="/wiki/Web_interface" class="mw-redirect" title="Web interface">web interface</a> and that maybe was requested by an <a href="/wiki/XMLHttpRequest" title="XMLHttpRequest">XMLHttpRequest</a> <a href="/wiki/API" title="API">API</a>) (see also: <a href="/wiki/Dynamic_web_page" title="Dynamic web page">dynamic page</a>).</li></ul>
<p>In practice whenever there is content that may vary, depending on one or more parameters contained in client request or in configuration settings, then, usually, it is generated dynamically.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Send_response_message">Send response message</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Web_server&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Send response message"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>Web server programs are able to send response messages as replies to client request messages.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-rfc7230-2.1&#95;29-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rfc7230-2.1-29"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>29<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>An error response message may be sent because a request message could not be successfully read or decoded or analyzed or executed.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-rfc7230-3.4&#95;30-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rfc7230-3.4-30"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>30<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>NOTE: the following sections are reported only as examples to help to understand what a web server, more or less, does; these sections are by any means neither exhaustive nor complete.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Error_message">Error message</h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Web_server&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Error message"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>A web server program may reply to a client request message with many kinds of error messages, anyway these errors are divided mainly in two categories:
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/HTTP_client_errors" class="mw-redirect" title="HTTP client errors">HTTP client errors</a>, due to the type of request message or to the availability of requested web resource;<sup id="cite&#95;ref-rfc7231-6.5&#95;38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rfc7231-6.5-38"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>38<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/HTTP_server_errors" class="mw-redirect" title="HTTP server errors">HTTP server errors</a>, due to internal server errors.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-rfc7231-6.6&#95;39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rfc7231-6.6-39"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>39<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li></ul>
<p>When an error response or message is received by a client browser, then if it is related to the main user request (e.g., an URL of a web resource such as a web page) then usually that error message is shown in some browser window or message.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="URL_authorization">URL authorization</h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Web_server&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: URL authorization"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>A web server program may be able to verify whether the requested URL path:<sup id="cite&#95;ref-rfc7235-1&#95;40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rfc7235-1-40"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>40<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<ul><li>can be freely accessed by everybody;</li>
<li>requires a user authentication (request of user credentials such as <a href="/wiki/User_name" class="mw-redirect" title="User name">user name</a> and <a href="/wiki/Password" title="Password">password</a>);</li>
<li>access is forbidden to some or all kind of users.</li></ul>
<p>If the authorization or access-rights feature has been implemented and enabled and access to web resource is not granted, then, depending on the required access rights, a web server program:
</p>
