<ul><li>can deny access by sending a specific error message (e.g., access <a href="/wiki/List_of_HTTP_status_codes#403" title="List of HTTP status codes">forbidden</a>);</li>
<li>may deny access by sending a specific error message (e.g., access <a href="/wiki/List_of_HTTP_status_codes#401" title="List of HTTP status codes">unauthorized</a>) that usually forces the client browser to ask human user to provide required user credentials; if authentication credentials are provided then web server program verifies and accepts or rejects them.</li></ul>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="URL_redirection">URL redirection</h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Web_server&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: URL redirection"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1320445320" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/URL_redirection" title="URL redirection">URL redirection</a></div>
<p>A web server program <i>may</i> have the capability of doing URL redirections to new URLs (new locations) which consists in replying to a client request message with a response message containing a new URL suited to access a valid or an existing web resource (client should redo the request with the new URL).<sup id="cite&#95;ref-rfc7231-6.4&#95;41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rfc7231-6.4-41"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>41<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>URL redirection of location is used:<sup id="cite&#95;ref-rfc7231-6.4&#95;41-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rfc7231-6.4-41"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>41<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<ul><li>to fix a directory name by adding a final slash '/';<sup id="cite&#95;ref-ws-directory-listings&#95;36-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ws-directory-listings-36"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>36<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li>to give a new URL for a no more existing URL path to a new path where that kind of web resource can be found.</li>
<li>to give a new URL to another domain when current domain has too much load.</li></ul>
<p>Example 1: a URL path points to a <b>directory</b> name but it does not have a final slash '/' so web server sends a redirect to client in order to instruct it to redo the request with the fixed path name.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-ws-directory-listings&#95;36-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ws-directory-listings-36"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>36<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>From:<br />
&#160;&#160;<code>/directory1/directory2</code><br />
To:<br />
&#160;&#160;<code>/directory1/directory2/</code>
</p><p>Example 2: a whole set of documents has been <b>moved inside website</b> in order to reorganize their file system paths.
</p><p>From:<br />
&#160;&#160;<code>/directory1/directory2/2021-10-08/</code><br />
To:<br />
&#160;&#160;<code>/directory1/directory2/2021/10/08/</code>
</p><p>Example 3: a whole set of documents has been <b>moved to a new website</b> and now it is mandatory to use secure HTTPS connections to access them.
</p><p>From:<br />
&#160;&#160;<code>http://www.example.com/directory1/directory2/2021-10-08/</code><br />
To:<br />
&#160;&#160;<code>https://docs.example.com/directory1/2021-10-08/</code>
</p><p>Above examples are only a few of the possible kind of redirections.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Successful_message">Successful message</h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Web_server&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Successful message"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>A web server program is able to reply to a valid client request message with a successful message, optionally containing requested <b>web resource data</b>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-rfc7231-6.3&#95;42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rfc7231-6.3-42"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>42<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>If web resource data is sent back to client, then it can be <b>static content</b> or <b>dynamic content</b> depending on how it has been retrieved (from a file or from the output of some program or module).
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Content_cache">Content cache</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Web_server&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Content cache"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>In order to speed up web server responses by lowering average HTTP response times and hardware resources used, many popular web servers implement one or more content <a href="/wiki/Cache_(computing)" title="Cache (computing)">caches</a>, each one specialized in a content category.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-ws-content-cache-apache&#95;43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ws-content-cache-apache-43"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>43<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
<sup id="cite&#95;ref-ws-content-cache-nginx&#95;44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ws-content-cache-nginx-44"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>44<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Content is usually cached by its origin:
</p>
<ul><li>static content:
<ul><li><a href="#File_cache">file cache</a>;</li></ul></li>
<li>dynamic content:
<ul><li><a href="#Dynamic_cache">dynamic cache</a> (module or program output).</li></ul></li></ul>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="File_cache">File cache</h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Web_server&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: File cache"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>Historically, static contents found in <a href="/wiki/Computer_file" title="Computer file">files</a> which had to be accessed frequently, randomly and quickly, have been stored mostly on electro-mechanical <a href="/wiki/Hard_disk_drive" title="Hard disk drive">disks</a> since mid-late 1960s and 1970s; regrettably reads from and writes to those kind of <a href="/wiki/Peripheral" title="Peripheral">devices</a> have always been considered very slow operations when compared to <a href="/wiki/RAM" class="mw-redirect" title="RAM">RAM</a> speed and so, since early <a href="/wiki/Operative_system" class="mw-redirect" title="Operative system">OSs</a>, first disk caches and then also <a href="/wiki/Operating_system" title="Operating system">OS</a> file <a href="/wiki/Cache_(computing)" title="Cache (computing)">cache</a> sub-systems were developed to speed up <a href="/wiki/Input/output" title="Input/output">I/O</a> operations of frequently accessed data.
</p><p>Even with the aid of an OS file cache, the relative or occasional slowness of I/O operations involving directories and files stored on disks became soon a <a href="/wiki/Bottleneck_(software)" title="Bottleneck (software)">bottleneck</a> in the increase of <a href="#Performances">performances</a> expected from top level web servers, specially since mid-late 1990s, when web Internet traffic started to grow exponentially along with the constant increase of speed of Internet or network lines.
</p><p>The problem about how to further efficiently speed-up the serving of static files, thus increasing the maximum number of requests or responses per second (<a href="#requests_per_second">RPS</a>), started to be studied and researched since mid 1990s, with the aim to propose useful cache models that could be implemented in web server programs.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-ws-file-cache-mmc&#95;45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ws-file-cache-mmc-45"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>45<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In practice, nowadays, many web server programs include their own <i><a href="/wiki/Userland_(computing)" class="mw-redirect" title="Userland (computing)">userland</a></i> <b>file cache</b>, tailored for a web server usage and using their specific implementation and parameters.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-ws-file-cache-iplanet&#95;46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ws-file-cache-iplanet-46"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>46<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
<sup id="cite&#95;ref-ws-file-cache-apache&#95;47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ws-file-cache-apache-47"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>47<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
<sup id="cite&#95;ref-ws-file-cache-servez&#95;48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ws-file-cache-servez-48"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>48<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The wide spread adoption of <a href="/wiki/Redundant_array_of_independent_disks" class="mw-redirect" title="Redundant array of independent disks">RAID</a> and fast <a href="/wiki/Solid-state_drive" title="Solid-state drive">solid-state drives</a> (storage hardware with very high I/O speed) has slightly reduced but of course not eliminated the advantage of having a file cache incorporated in a web server.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Dynamic_cache">Dynamic cache</h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Web_server&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Dynamic cache"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>Dynamic content, output by an internal module or an external program, may not always change very frequently (given a unique URL with keys or parameters) and so, maybe for a while (e.g., from one second to several hours or more), the resulting output can be cached in RAM or even on a fast <a href="/wiki/Disk_storage" title="Disk storage">disk</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-ws-disk-cache-apache&#95;49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ws-disk-cache-apache-49"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>49<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The typical usage of a dynamic cache is when a website has <a href="/wiki/Dynamic_web_page" title="Dynamic web page">dynamic web pages</a> about news, weather, images, maps, etc. that do not change frequently (e.g., every <i>n</i> minutes) and that are accessed by a huge number of clients per minute per hour; in those cases it is useful to return cached content too (without calling the internal module or the external program) because clients often do not have an updated copy of the requested content in their browser caches.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-ws-dynamic-cache-edu&#95;50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ws-dynamic-cache-edu-50"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>50<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Anyway, in most cases those kind of caches are implemented by external servers (e.g., <a href="/wiki/Reverse_proxy" title="Reverse proxy">reverse proxy</a>) or by storing dynamic data output in separate computers, managed by specific applications (e.g., <a href="/wiki/Memcached" title="Memcached">memcached</a>), in order to not compete for hardware resources (CPU, RAM, disks) with web servers.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-ws-dynamic-cache-tut&#95;51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ws-dynamic-cache-tut-51"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>51<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
<sup id="cite&#95;ref-ws-dynamic-cache-std&#95;52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ws-dynamic-cache-std-52"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>52<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Kernel-mode_and_user-mode_web_servers">Kernel-mode and user-mode web servers</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Web_server&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Kernel-mode and user-mode web servers"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>A web server software can be either incorporated into the <a href="/wiki/Operating_system" title="Operating system">OS</a> and executed in <a href="/wiki/Kernel_(operating_system)" title="Kernel (operating system)">kernel</a> space, or it can be executed in <a href="/wiki/User_space" class="mw-redirect" title="User space">user space</a> (like other regular applications).
</p><p>Web servers that run in <a href="/wiki/Supervisor_mode" class="mw-redirect" title="Supervisor mode">kernel mode</a> (usually called <a href="/wiki/In-kernel_web_server" title="In-kernel web server">kernel space web servers</a>) can have direct access to kernel resources and so they can be, in theory, faster than those running in user mode, but there are disadvantages in running a web server in kernel mode (e.g., difficulties in developing and <a href="/wiki/Debugging" title="Debugging">debugging</a> software) whereas <a href="/wiki/Runtime_(program_lifecycle_phase)" class="mw-redirect" title="Runtime (program lifecycle phase)">run-time</a> <a href="/wiki/Critical_error" class="mw-redirect" title="Critical error">critical errors</a> may lead to serious problems in OS kernel.
</p><p>Web servers that run in <a href="/wiki/User-mode" class="mw-redirect" title="User-mode">user-mode</a> have to ask the system for permission to use more memory or more <a href="/wiki/Central_processing_unit" title="Central processing unit">CPU</a> resources. Not only do these requests to the kernel take time, but they might not always be satisfied because the system reserves resources for its own usage and has the responsibility to share hardware resources with all the other running applications. Executing in user mode can also mean using more buffer or data copies (between user-space and kernel-space) which can lead to a decrease in the performance of a user-mode web server.
</p><p>Nowadays almost all web server software is executed in user mode (because many of the aforementioned small disadvantages have been overcome by faster hardware, new OS versions, much faster OS <a href="/wiki/System_calls" class="mw-redirect" title="System calls">system calls</a> and new optimized web server software). See also <a href="/wiki/Comparison_of_web_server_software" title="Comparison of web server software">comparison of web server software</a> to discover which of them run in kernel mode or in user mode (also referred as kernel space or user space).
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Performances">Performances</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Web_server&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Performances"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>To <b>improve the <a href="/wiki/User_experience" title="User experience">user experience</a></b> (on client or browser side), a web server should <b>reply quickly</b> (as soon as possible) to client requests; unless content response is throttled (by configuration) for some type of files (e.g., big or huge files), also returned data content should be sent as fast as possible (high transfer speed).
</p><p>In other words, a <b>web server should always be very <a href="/wiki/Responsiveness" title="Responsiveness">responsive</a></b>, even under high load of web traffic, in order to keep <b>total user's wait</b> (sum of browser time + network time + <b>web server response time</b>) for a response <b>as low as possible</b>.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Performance_metrics">Performance metrics</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Web_server&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Performance metrics"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>For web server software, main key <b>performance metrics</b> (measured under vary <a href="#Operating_conditions">operating conditions</a>) usually are at least the following ones:<sup id="cite&#95;ref-first-monday-web-server-performance&#95;53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-first-monday-web-server-performance-53"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>53<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<ul><li><strong>number of <i><style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1238216509">.mw-parser-output .vanchor>:target~.vanchor-text{background-color:#b1d2ff}@media screen{html.skin-theme-clientpref-night .mw-parser-output .vanchor>:target~.vanchor-text{background-color:#0f4dc9}}@media screen and (prefers-color-scheme:dark){html.skin-theme-clientpref-os .mw-parser-output .vanchor>:target~.vanchor-text{background-color:#0f4dc9}}</style><span class="vanchor"><span id="requests&#95;per&#95;second"></span><span class="vanchor-text">requests per second</span></span></i></strong> (<strong>RPS</strong>, similar to <strong><a href="/wiki/Queries_per_second" title="Queries per second">QPS</a></strong>, depending on HTTP version and configuration, type of HTTP requests and other operating conditions);</li>
<li><strong>number of <i>connections per second</i></strong> (<strong>CPS</strong>), is the number of connections per second accepted by web server (useful when using HTTP/1.0 or HTTP/1.1 with a very low limit of requests or responses per connection, i.e., 1 .. 20);</li>
<li><strong><a href="/wiki/Network_latency" class="mw-redirect" title="Network latency">network latency</a></strong> + <b><a href="/wiki/Response_time_(technology)" title="Response time (technology)">response time</a></b> for each new client request; usually benchmark tool shows how many requests have been satisfied within a scale of time laps (e.g., within 1ms, 3ms, 5ms, 10ms, 20ms, 30ms, 40ms) or the shortest, the average and the longest response time;</li>
<li><strong><a href="/wiki/Throughput" class="mw-redirect" title="Throughput">throughput</a> of responses</strong>, in bytes per second.</li></ul>
<p>Among the operating conditions, the <strong>number</strong> (1 .. <i>n</i>) of <strong>concurrent client connections</strong> used during a test is an important parameter because it allows to correlate the <strong><a href="/wiki/Concurrency_(computer_science)" title="Concurrency (computer science)">concurrency</a> level</strong> supported by web server with results of the tested performance metrics.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Software_efficiency">Software efficiency</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Web_server&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Software efficiency"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>The <b>specific web server <a href="/wiki/Software_design" title="Software design">software design</a> and model adopted</b>:
</p>
<ul><li>single <a href="/wiki/Process_(computing)" title="Process (computing)">process</a> or multi-process;</li>
<li>single <a href="/wiki/Thread_(computing)" title="Thread (computing)">thread</a> (no thread) or multi-thread for each process;</li>
<li>usage of <a href="/wiki/Coroutines" class="mw-redirect" title="Coroutines">coroutines</a> or not;</li></ul>
<p>... and other <b>programming techniques</b>, such as:
</p>
<ul><li>minimization of possible <a href="/wiki/Cache_miss" class="mw-redirect" title="Cache miss">CPU cache misses</a>;</li>
<li>minimization of possible <a href="/wiki/Branch_misprediction" class="mw-redirect" title="Branch misprediction">CPU branch mispredictions</a> in critical paths for speed;</li>
<li>minimization of the number of <a href="/wiki/System_call" title="System call">system calls</a> used to perform a certain function or task;</li>
<li>other tricks;</li></ul>
<p>... used to implement a web server program, <b>can bias a lot the <a href="/wiki/Computer_performance" title="Computer performance">performances</a></b> and in particular the <b><a href="/wiki/Scalability" title="Scalability">scalability</a> level</b> that can be achieved under <b>heavy load</b> or when using high end hardware (many CPUs, disks and lots of RAM).
</p><p>In practice some web server software models may require more OS resources (specially more CPUs and more RAM) than others to be able to work well and so to achieve target performances.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Operating_conditions">Operating conditions</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Web_server&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Operating conditions"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>There are many <b>operating conditions that can affect the performances</b> of a web server; performance values may vary depending on:
</p>
<ul><li>the settings of web server (including the fact that log file is or is not enabled, etc.);</li>
<li>the HTTP version used by client requests;</li>
<li>the average HTTP request type (method, length of HTTP headers and optional body);</li>
<li>whether the requested content is static or dynamic;</li>
<li>whether the content is <a href="/wiki/Web_cache" title="Web cache">cached</a> or not cached (by server or client);</li>
<li>whether the content is <a href="/wiki/HTTP_compression" title="HTTP compression">compressed</a> on the fly (when transferred), pre-compressed (i.e., when a file resource is stored on disk already compressed so that web server can send that file directly to the network with the only indication that its content is compressed) or not compressed at all;</li>
<li>whether the connections are or are not encrypted;</li>
<li>the average <a href="/wiki/Network_speed" class="mw-redirect" title="Network speed">network speed</a> between web server and its clients;</li>
<li>the number of active <a href="/wiki/Transmission_control_protocol" class="mw-redirect" title="Transmission control protocol">TCP</a> connections;</li>
<li>the number of active processes managed by web server (including external CGI, SCGI, FCGI programs);</li>
<li>the <a href="/wiki/Computer_hardware" title="Computer hardware">hardware</a> and <a href="/wiki/Computer_software" class="mw-redirect" title="Computer software">software</a> limitations or settings of the <a href="/wiki/Operating_system" title="Operating system">OS</a> of the computers on which the web server runs;</li>
<li>other minor conditions.</li></ul>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Benchmarking">Benchmarking</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Web_server&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Benchmarking"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1320445320" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Web_server_benchmarking" title="Web server benchmarking">Web server benchmarking</a></div>
<p>Performances of a web server are typically <a href="/wiki/Benchmark_(computing)" title="Benchmark (computing)">benchmarked</a> by using one or more of the available
<a href="/wiki/Web_server_benchmarking#Tools_for_benchmarking" title="Web server benchmarking">automated load testing tools</a>.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Load_limits">Load limits</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Web_server&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Load limits"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>A web server (program installation) usually has pre-defined <b>load limits</b> for each combination of <a href="#Operating_conditions">operating conditions</a>, also because it is limited by OS resources and because it can handle only a limited number of concurrent client connections (usually between 2 and several tens of thousands for each active web server process, see also the <a href="/wiki/C10k_problem" title="C10k problem">C10k problem</a> and the <a href="/wiki/C10M_problem" class="mw-redirect" title="C10M problem">C10M problem</a>).
</p><p>When a web server is near to or over its load limits, it gets <b>overloaded</b> and so it may become <b>unresponsive</b>.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Causes_of_overload">Causes of overload</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Web_server&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Causes of overload"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>At any time web servers can be overloaded due to one or more of the following causes:
</p>
<ul><li><b>Excess legitimate web traffic</b>. Thousands or even millions of clients connecting to the website in a short amount of time (e.g., the <a href="/wiki/Slashdot_effect" title="Slashdot effect">Slashdot effect</a>).</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Distributed_Denial_of_Service" class="mw-redirect" title="Distributed Denial of Service">Distributed Denial of Service</a> attacks. A denial-of-service attack (DoS attack) or distributed denial-of-service attack (DDoS attack) is an attempt to make a computer or network resource unavailable to its intended users.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Computer_worm" title="Computer worm">Computer worms</a> that sometimes cause abnormal traffic because of millions of infected computers (not coordinated among them).</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/XSS_worm" title="XSS worm">XSS worms</a> can cause high traffic because of millions of infected browsers or web servers.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Internet_bot" title="Internet bot">Internet bots</a> Traffic not filtered or limited on large websites with very few network resources (e.g., <a href="/wiki/Bandwidth_(computing)" title="Bandwidth (computing)">bandwidth</a>) or hardware resources (CPUs, RAM, disks).</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Internet" title="Internet">Internet</a> (network) slowdowns (e.g., due to packet losses) so that client requests are served more slowly and the number of connections increases so much that server limits are reached.</li>
<li>Web servers, <b>serving dynamic content</b>, <b>waiting for slow responses coming from <a href="/wiki/Front_and_back_ends" class="mw-redirect" title="Front and back ends">back-end</a> computers</b> (e.g., <a href="/wiki/Database" title="Database">databases</a>), maybe because of too many queries mixed with too many inserts or updates of DB data; in these cases web servers have to wait for back-end data responses before replying to HTTP clients but during these waits too many new client connections or requests arrive and so they become overloaded.</li>
<li>Web servers (<a href="/wiki/Computer" title="Computer">computers</a>) <b>partial unavailability</b>. This can happen because of required or urgent maintenance or upgrade, hardware or software failures such as <a href="/wiki/Front_and_back_ends" class="mw-redirect" title="Front and back ends">back-end</a> (e.g., <a href="/wiki/Database" title="Database">database</a>) failures; in these cases the remaining web servers may get too much traffic and become overloaded.</li></ul>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Symptoms_of_overload">Symptoms of overload</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Web_server&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Symptoms of overload"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>The symptoms of an overloaded web server are usually the following ones:
</p>
<ul><li>Requests are served with (possibly long) delays (from one second to a few hundred seconds).</li>
<li>The web server returns an <a href="/wiki/List_of_HTTP_status_codes" title="List of HTTP status codes">HTTP error code</a>, such as 500, 502,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>54<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>55<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> 503,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>56<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> 504,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>57<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> 408, or even an intermittent <a href="/wiki/HTTP_404" title="HTTP 404">404</a>.</li>
<li>The web server refuses or resets (interrupts) <a href="/wiki/Transmission_control_protocol" class="mw-redirect" title="Transmission control protocol">TCP</a> connections before it returns any content.</li>
<li>In very rare cases, the web server returns only a part of the requested content. This behavior can be considered a <a href="/wiki/Software_bug" title="Software bug">bug</a>, even if it usually arises as a symptom of overload.</li></ul>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Anti-overload_techniques">Anti-overload techniques</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Web_server&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Anti-overload techniques"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>To partially overcome above average load limits and to prevent overload, most popular websites use common techniques like the following ones:
</p>
<ul><li>Tuning OS parameters for hardware capabilities and usage.</li>
<li>Tuning web servers parameters to improve their security and performances.</li>
<li>Deploying <strong><a href="/wiki/Web_cache" title="Web cache">web cache</a></strong> techniques (not only for static contents but, whenever possible, for dynamic contents too).</li>
<li>Managing network traffic, by using:
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Firewall_(computing)" title="Firewall (computing)">Firewalls</a> to block unwanted traffic coming from bad IP sources or having bad patterns;</li>
<li>HTTP traffic managers to drop, redirect or rewrite requests having bad <a href="/wiki/HTTP" title="HTTP">HTTP</a> patterns;</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Bandwidth_management" title="Bandwidth management">Bandwidth management</a> and <a href="/wiki/Traffic_shaping" title="Traffic shaping">traffic shaping</a>, in order to smooth down peaks in network usage.</li></ul></li>
<li>Using different <a href="/wiki/Domain_name" title="Domain name">domain names</a>, <a href="/wiki/IP_address" title="IP address">IP addresses</a> and computers to serve different kinds (static and dynamic) of content; the aim is to <b>separate</b> big or huge files (<code>download.*</code>) (that domain might be replaced also by a <a href="/wiki/Content_delivery_network" title="Content delivery network">CDN</a>) from small and medium-sized files (<code>static.*</code>) and from main dynamic site (maybe where some contents are stored in a <a href="/wiki/Back-end_database" title="Back-end database">backend database</a>) (<code>www.*</code>); the idea is to be able to efficiently serve big or huge (over 10 – 1000 MB) files (maybe throttling downloads) and to fully <a href="/wiki/Web_cache" title="Web cache">cache</a> small and medium-sized files, without affecting performances of dynamic site under heavy load, by using different settings for each (group) of web server computers:
<ul><li><code>https://download.example.com</code></li>
<li><code>https://static.example.com</code></li>
<li><code>https://www.example.com</code></li></ul></li>
<li>Using many web servers (computers) that are grouped together behind a <a href="/wiki/Load_balancing_(computing)" title="Load balancing (computing)">load balancer</a> so that they act or are seen as one big web server.</li>
<li>Adding more hardware resources (i.e., <a href="/wiki/Random-access_memory" title="Random-access memory">RAM</a>, fast <a href="/wiki/Disk_storage" title="Disk storage">disks</a>) to each computer.</li>
<li>Using more efficient computer programs for web servers (see also: <a href="#Software_efficiency">software efficiency</a>).</li>
<li>Using the most efficient <strong><a href="#StandardCGIs">Web Server Gateway Interface</a></strong> to process dynamic requests (spawning one or more external programs every time a dynamic page is retrieved, kills performances).</li>
<li>Using other programming techniques and <a href="/wiki/Workaround" title="Workaround">workarounds</a>, especially if dynamic content is involved, to speed up the HTTP responses (i.e., by avoiding dynamic calls to retrieve objects, such as style sheets, images and scripts), that never change or change very rarely, by copying that content to static files once and then keeping them synchronized with dynamic content.</li>
<li>Using latest efficient versions of <a href="/wiki/Hypertext_Transfer_Protocol" class="mw-redirect" title="Hypertext Transfer Protocol">HTTP</a> (e.g., beyond using common HTTP/1.1 also by enabling <a href="/wiki/HTTP/2" title="HTTP/2">HTTP/2</a> and maybe <a href="/wiki/HTTP/3" title="HTTP/3">HTTP/3</a> too, whenever available web server software has reliable support for the latter two protocols) in order to reduce a lot the number of TCP/IP connections started by each client and the size of data exchanged (because of more compact HTTP headers representation and maybe data compression). This may not prevent overloads of RAM and CPU caused by the need for encryption. It may also not address overloads caused by excessively large files uploaded at high speed, because they are optimized for concurrency.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-nextcloud-http2-slow-upload&#95;58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nextcloud-http2-slow-upload-58"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>58<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-nginx-http2-slow-upload&#95;59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nginx-http2-slow-upload-59"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>59<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li></ul>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Market_share">Market share</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Web_server&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Market share"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1320445320" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information&#32;on HTTP server programs: <a href="/wiki/Category:Web_server_software" title="Category:Web server software">Category:Web server software</a></div>
<figure class="mw-halign-right" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Usage_share_of_web_servers_(Source_Netcraft).svg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Usage_share_of_web_servers_%28Source_Netcraft%29.svg/330px-Usage_share_of_web_servers_%28Source_Netcraft%29.svg.png" decoding="async" width="300" height="175" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Usage_share_of_web_servers_%28Source_Netcraft%29.svg/500px-Usage_share_of_web_servers_%28Source_Netcraft%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Usage_share_of_web_servers_%28Source_Netcraft%29.svg/960px-Usage_share_of_web_servers_%28Source_Netcraft%29.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1080" data-file-height="630" /></a><figcaption>Chart:<br /><i>Market share of all sites</i> for most popular web servers 2005–2021</figcaption></figure>

<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="See_also">See also</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Web_server&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: See also"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>

<li><a href="/wiki/Variant_object" title="Variant object">Variant object</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Virtual_hosting" title="Virtual hosting">Virtual hosting</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Web_hosting_service" title="Web hosting service">Web hosting service</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Web_container" title="Web container">Web container</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Web_proxy" class="mw-redirect" title="Web proxy">Web proxy</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Web_service" title="Web service">Web service</a></li></ul>
<p><span class="anchor" id="StandardCGIs"></span><b>Standard Web Server Gateway Interfaces used for <a href="/wiki/Dynamic_content" class="mw-redirect" title="Dynamic content">dynamic contents</a>:</b>
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Common_Gateway_Interface" title="Common Gateway Interface">CGI</a> Common Gateway Interface</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Simple_Common_Gateway_Interface" title="Simple Common Gateway Interface">SCGI</a> Simple Common Gateway Interface</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/FastCGI" title="FastCGI">FastCGI</a> Fast Common Gateway Interface</li></ul>
<p><span class="anchor" id="CustomCGIs"></span><b>A few other Web Server Interfaces (server or <a href="/wiki/Programming_language" title="Programming language">programming language</a> specific) used for dynamic contents:</b>
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Server_Side_Includes" title="Server Side Includes">SSI</a> Server Side Includes, rarely used, static HTML documents containing SSI directives are interpreted by server software to include small dynamic data on the fly when pages are served (e.g., date and time, other static file contents, etc.).</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Server_application_programming_interface" title="Server application programming interface">SAPI</a> Server Application Programming Interface:
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/ISAPI" class="mw-redirect" title="ISAPI">ISAPI</a> Internet Server Application Programming Interface</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Netscape_Server_Application_Programming_Interface" title="Netscape Server Application Programming Interface">NSAPI</a> Netscape Server Application Programming Interface</li></ul></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/PSGI" class="mw-redirect" title="PSGI">PSGI</a> Perl Web Server Gateway Interface</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/WSGI" class="mw-redirect" title="WSGI">WSGI</a> Python Web Server Gateway Interface</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Rack_(web_server_interface)" title="Rack (web server interface)">Rack</a> Rack Web Server Gateway Interface</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/JSGI" title="JSGI">JSGI</a> JavaScript Web Server Gateway Interface</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Java_Servlet" class="mw-redirect" title="Java Servlet">Java Servlet</a>, <a href="/wiki/JavaServer_Pages" class="mw-redirect" title="JavaServer Pages">JavaServer Pages</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Active_Server_Pages" title="Active Server Pages">Active Server Pages</a>, <a href="/wiki/ASP.NET" title="ASP.NET">ASP.NET</a></li></ul>
